      <p><b>Elizabeth Montague Ryan</b> (February 5, 1892 – July 6, 1979) was an American <a href="/wiki/Tennis" title="Tennis">tennis</a> player who was born in <a href="/wiki/Anaheim,_California" title="Anaheim, California">Anaheim, California</a> but lived most of her life in the United Kingdom. Ryan won 26 <a href="/wiki/Grand_Slam_(tennis)" title="Grand Slam (tennis)">Grand Slam</a> titles. Nineteen of those titles were in women's doubles and mixed doubles at <a href="/wiki/Wimbledon_Championships" class="mw-redirect" title="Wimbledon Championships">Wimbledon</a>, an all-time record for those two events. Twelve of her Wimbledon titles were in women's doubles and seven were in mixed doubles. Ryan also won four women's doubles titles at the <a href="/wiki/French_Open" title="French Open">French Championships</a>, as well as one women's doubles title and two mixed doubles titles at the <a href="/wiki/US_Open_(tennis)" title="US Open (tennis)">U.S. Championships</a>. </p>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Career">Career</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Elizabeth_Ryan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Career">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <p>Although she reached the Wimbledon singles finals twice, Ryan never won the title. Eight of her losses at Wimbledon were to players generally considered to be among the best ever. Ryan had to play <a href="/wiki/Dorothea_Lambert_Chambers" class="mw-redirect" title="Dorothea Lambert Chambers">Dorothea Lambert Chambers</a> in the all-comers final of 1920; <a href="/wiki/Suzanne_Lenglen" title="Suzanne Lenglen">Suzanne Lenglen</a> in the 1919 semifinals (losing 6–4, 7–5), 1921 final, 1922 quarterfinals, 1924 quarterfinals (losing 6–2, 6–8, 6–4), and 1925 second round; and <a href="/wiki/Helen_Wills_Moody" class="mw-redirect" title="Helen Wills Moody">Helen Wills Moody</a> in the 1928 semifinals and 1930 final. </p>
      <p>In the 1926 singles final at the U.S. Championships, the 34-year-old Ryan led 42-year-old <a href="/wiki/Molla_Bjurstedt_Mallory" class="mw-redirect" title="Molla Bjurstedt Mallory">Molla Bjurstedt Mallory</a> 4–6, 6–4, 4–0 and had a match point at 7–6 in the third set before losing the final three games of the match.<sup id="cite_ref-Collins's_Ryan_entry_1-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Collins's_Ryan_entry-1">[1]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Ryan and her longtime partner Lenglen never lost a women's doubles match at Wimbledon, going 31–0.<sup id="cite_ref-Collins's_Ryan_entry_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Collins's_Ryan_entry-1">[1]</a></sup> Only <a href="/wiki/Billie_Jean_King" title="Billie Jean King">Billie Jean King</a> (224 match wins) and <a href="/wiki/Martina_Navratilova" title="Martina Navratilova">Martina Navratilova</a> won more matches at Wimbledon than Ryan (190 match wins): 47–15 in singles, 73–4 in women's doubles, and 70–9 in mixed doubles.<sup id="cite_ref-Collins's_Ryan_entry_1-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Collins's_Ryan_entry-1">[1]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The longtime tennis writer <a href="/wiki/Ted_Tinling" title="Ted Tinling">Ted Tinling</a> has credited Ryan with inventing the volleying style later perfected by players such as <a href="/wiki/Sarah_Palfrey_Cooke" title="Sarah Palfrey Cooke">Sarah Palfrey Cooke</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alice_Marble" title="Alice Marble">Alice Marble</a>, <a href="/wiki/Louise_Brough_Clapp" class="mw-redirect" title="Louise Brough Clapp">Louise Brough Clapp</a>, <a href="/wiki/Margaret_Osborne_duPont" title="Margaret Osborne duPont">Margaret Osborne duPont</a>, <a href="/wiki/Doris_Hart" title="Doris Hart">Doris Hart</a>, <a href="/wiki/Darlene_Hard" title="Darlene Hard">Darlene Hard</a>, <a href="/wiki/Margaret_Court" title="Margaret Court">Margaret Court</a>, Navratilova, and King. "Before World War I, women's tennis consisted primary of slogging duels from the baseline. There were a few volleying pioneers, notably ... <a href="/wiki/Hazel_Hotchkiss_Wightman" title="Hazel Hotchkiss Wightman">Hazel [Hotchkiss] Wightman</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ethel_Thomson_Larcombe" title="Ethel Thomson Larcombe">Ethel [Thomson] Larcombe</a>, but volleying as a fundamental, aggressive technique was first injected into the women's game by ... Ryan."<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup> Tinling, however, also said about Ryan, "Elizabeth wasn't fast enough for singles. Too heavy."<sup id="cite_ref-Collins,_Bud_1989_261_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Collins,_Bud_1989_261-3">[3]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>According to Wallis Myers of <a href="/wiki/Daily_Telegraph" class="mw-redirect" title="Daily Telegraph">The Daily Telegraph</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Daily_Mail" title="Daily Mail">Daily Mail</a>, Ryan was ranked in the world top ten from 1921 (when the rankings began) through 1928 and again in 1930, reaching a career high of World No. 3 in those rankings in 1927.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup> Ryan was ranked second behind Mallory in the year-end rankings issued by the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Tennis_Association" title="United States Tennis Association">United States Lawn Tennis Association</a> for 1925 and 1926.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Ryan died on July 6, 1979, at age 87, on the grounds of the <a href="/wiki/All_England_Lawn_Tennis_and_Croquet_Club" title="All England Lawn Tennis and Croquet Club">All England Lawn Tennis and Croquet Club</a> at Wimbledon, following the ladies singes final and the day before King broke her record number of Wimbledon wins by winning her 20th title.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-wot1980_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wot1980-8">[8]</a></sup> When tennis writer and television commentator <a href="/wiki/Bud_Collins" title="Bud Collins">Bud Collins</a> tried to arrange for Ryan and King to film an interview together at Wimbledon in 1979, Ryan refused.<sup id="cite_ref-Collins,_Bud_1989_261_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Collins,_Bud_1989_261-3">[3]</a></sup> King said, "I always liked seeing Miss Ryan at Wimbledon, and I'd try to be friendly, but she didn't seem to want it. For me, it wasn't personal. Sure, I wanted the record, but I wasn't trying to steal a possession of hers."<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup> King also said, "[T]here is no doubt in my mind that she just didn't want to be alive to see her record broken. She was [87], she had held it for a long, long time and she wanted it for herself. But records are there to be broken."<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> </p>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Grand_Slam_tournament_timelines">Grand Slam tournament timelines</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Elizabeth_Ryan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Grand Slam tournament timelines">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <table border="1px" style="border-collapse:collapse; border-color:#aaa; margin-bottom:0.5em;" cellpadding="5" cellspacing="0"> 
       <caption style="text-align:left">
        <b>Key</b> 
       </caption> 
       <tbody>
        <tr> 
         <td style="background:#00ff00"><b><abbr title="Won tournament">W</abbr></b> </td> 
         <td style="background:#D8BFD8">&nbsp;<abbr title="Reached final">F</abbr>&nbsp; </td> 
         <td style="background:yellow"><abbr title="Reached semifinal">SF</abbr> </td> 
         <td style="background:#ffebcd"><abbr title="Reached quarterfinal">QF</abbr> </td> 
         <td style="background:#afeeee"><abbr title="Out in earlier round">#R</abbr> </td> 
         <td style="background:#afeeee"><abbr title="Round-robin">RR</abbr> </td> 
         <td><abbr title="Out in qualification round">Q#</abbr> </td> 
         <td><abbr title="Absent">A</abbr> </td> 
         <td><abbr title="Tournament not held">NH</abbr> </td>
        </tr>

      <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r886047268">.mw-parser-output .refbegin{font-size:90%;margin-bottom:0.5em}.mw-parser-output .refbegin-hanging-indents>ul{list-style-type:none;margin-left:0}.mw-parser-output .refbegin-hanging-indents>ul>li,.mw-parser-output .refbegin-hanging-indents>dl>dd{margin-left:0;padding-left:3.2em;text-indent:-3.2em;list-style:none}.mw-parser-output .refbegin-100{font-size:100%}</style>
      <div class="refbegin" style="">
       (W) Won; (F) finalist; (SF) semifinalist; (QF) quarterfinalist; (#R) rounds 4, 3, 2, 1; (RR) round-robin stage; (Q#) qualification round; (A) absent; (NH) not held. SR=strike rate (events won/competed)

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Elizabeth_Ryan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <ul>
       <li><a href="/wiki/Tennis_performance_timeline_comparison_(women)" title="Tennis performance timeline comparison (women)">Performance timelines for all female tennis players who reached at least one Grand Slam or Olympic singles final</a></li>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Elizabeth_Ryan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: lower-alpha;"> 
       <div class="mw-references-wrap">
        <ol class="references"> 
         <li id="cite_note-french-11"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-french_11-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-french_11-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-french_11-2"><sup><i><b>c</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text">Through 1923, the French Championships were open only to French nationals. The World Hard Court Championships (WHCC), actually played on clay in Paris or Brussels, began in 1912 and were open to all nationalities. The results from that tournament are shown here from 1912 through 1914 and from 1920 through 1923. The Olympics replaced the WHCC in 1924, as the Olympics were held in Paris. Beginning in 1925, the French Championships were open to all nationalities, with the results shown here beginning with that year.</span> </li> 
        </ol>
       </div>
      </div>

      <div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: decimal;">
